  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_779aea18-caee-4780-bc68-3e77a1d24caa'
      });

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer3071506154848273491">Talita Luna<br/>Kesejatian hidup ada pada batu kerikil yang tertendang ketika kau melangkah<br/>menyusuri jalan. Kesejatian hidup ada pada selembar daun kering yang gugur<br/>tertiup angin. Kesejatian hidup ada air susu ibu yang yang merelakan puting<br/>payudaranya diisap oleh bayi manapun. Di<br/>Vihara Pit Yong Kiong, Pasuruan, di pelabuhan Belawan, di Penang, di<br/>Bangkok, di Laos, di Golden Tria</span>
  <span id="freeText3071506154848273491" style="display:none">Talita Luna<br />Kesejatian hidup ada pada batu kerikil yang tertendang ketika kau melangkah<br />menyusuri jalan. Kesejatian hidup ada pada selembar daun kering yang gugur<br />tertiup angin. Kesejatian hidup ada air susu ibu yang yang merelakan puting<br />payudaranya diisap oleh bayi manapun. Di<br />Vihara Pit Yong Kiong, Pasuruan, di pelabuhan Belawan, di Penang, di<br />Bangkok, di Laos, di Golden Triangle, di Cambodia, di Bandung, di<br />manapun kau hidup.<br /><br />Tapi, dia mungkin tak terlihat pada arus politik yang menyudutkanmu pada<br />pilihan kedigdayaan. Dia menyembunyikan diri dari teriakan-<br />teriakan yang menggemakan perubahan. Kesejatian hidup tak memerlukan<br />perubahan, namun juga tak menampiknya. Dia rebah pada semua kesederhanaan<br />yang ada di sekelilingmu. Maka, carilah, dan kamu akan mendapatinya.<br />Ketuklah, maka pintu akan dibukakan bagimu. Mintalah, maka kau akan diberi.<br /><br />Demikianlah Dewi Lestari mewakilkan sebuah upaya pencarian kesejatian hidup<br />pada seorang tokoh bernama Bodhi. Seorang bayi yang di suatu pagi tergeletak<br />di pintu Vihara. Dipungut, diasuh, dan dididik oleh seorang Pandita, Guru<br />Liong. Merasa bahwa karma pada hidup masa lalunya sangat berat. 18 tahun<br />dididik dengan ketat, termasuk penguasaan terhadap sebuah ilmu bela diri,<br />Bodhi mengalami penyempurnaan bathin. Pemurnian spirit. Termasuk sejumlah<br />pengalaman uniknya yang "merasa" menjadi ulat, tikus got, kucing, dan sapi.<br /><br />18 tahun adalah waktu yang cukup, dan Bodhi mohon pamit. Bersama serombongan<br />pendeta Buddha, Bodhi menyeberang ke Sumatera dan memutuskan menetap di<br />daerah Belawan. Tanpa KTP, tak juga faham mengenai asal usul dan tanggal<br />kelahirannya. Bekerja tiga bulan, mendapat upah, dan dibantu oleh Ompu<br />Berlin untuk mendapatkan sejumlah dokumen identitas termasuk paspor, Bodhi<br />menyeberang ke Penang. Disana dia bertemu dengan sejumlah backpackers yang<br />kemudian "memberi" arah perjalanan berikutnya: Bangkok.<br /><br />Bangkok surga bagi para backpackers. Ratusan pengelana dari mancanegara<br />tumpah di sana. Bodhi tinggal di semua rumah penginapan Srinthip bersama<br />sejumlah backpakers multi etnis. Penghuninya datang dan pergi. Masuklah<br />Kell, seorang lelaki tampan, peranakan Irlandia dan Mesir. Lelaki tertampan<br />yang mungkin pernah ada di bumi ini yang mempunyai tugas kehidupan untuk<br />membubuhkan 617 tatto pada 617 orang untuk membuat dirinya menyongsong<br />kemerdekaan paripurna setelah orang ke-617 membubuhkan tato yang ke-618 ke<br />tubuhnya. Lelaki yang kerap menyenandungkan Eye in The Sky-nya Alan Parson<br />Project. Kell kemudian mengajarinya tattoo. Lalu, jadilah Bodhi seorang<br />tattooist dan menjadikan itu sebagai cara untuk mendapatkan uang bagi biaya<br />hidup sehari-hari.<br /><br />Seorang backpacker perempuan bernama Star, berasal dari Hollywood, peranakan<br />Eropa Timur dan Timur Tengah masuk dan menginap di Srinthip. Perempuan<br />cantik dan tercantik yang pernah dilihat Bodhi. Perawakan tubuhnya sempurna.<br />Perempuan inilah yang memperkenalkan dirinya dengan sebuah perasaan lain<br />yang belum pernah dia rasakan sepanjang hidup. Star minta Bodhi mentattoonya<br />tepat di payudara.Dan bergetarlah kulit semesta. Bergerolalah gelombang<br />samudera. Erangan kesakitan Star sewaktu ditattoo adalah hasrat dedaunan<br />yang mendambakan sapuan sinar matahari. Waktu berlalu dan mereka berpisah.<br />Entah kenapa.<br /><br />Bodhi meneruskan pencarian kesejatiannya. Star seolah menggenap kesempurnaan<br />tattoonya dan pergi menyongsong kelana berikut.<br />Keterserakan yang tak menyenangkan. Tapi hidup adalah keping-keping misteri<br />yang baru terbuka setelah rebah sepenuhnya. Bodhi membiarkan semesta<br />menuntun perjalanan selanjutnya. Bertemu dengan lelaki tua pengasuh Bob<br />Marley, yang mengumandangkan reggae seolah cuma itu yang ada di bumi dan<br />kahyangan. Bertemu kembali dengan Tristan, backpacker yang ditemuinya<br />pertama kali di Penang. Mereka berdua bekerja di ladang ganja di Golden<br />Triangle dengan upah USD 700 per minggu. Sekian bulan di sana Bodhi memiliki<br />cukup uang untuk melanjutkan kembara berikutnya. Pulang ke Srinthip<br />didapatinya Kell sudah tak ada. Ah, lelaki yang telah memberinya keceriaan<br />dan sebuah warna baru.<br /><br />Rasa kangennya memuncak. Diputuskannya untuk pergi mencari Kell. Tak ada<br />petunjuk. Tak ada berita. Dan dia pergi. Suara semesta dan kerinduannya<br />adalah dua buah kompas sejati yang dia percaya akan mengantarkannya tepat<br />waktu - tepat arah kepada Kell. Bodhi terdampar di sebuah pertarungan antar<br />manusia ala Golden Triangle ditonton oleh ribuan petaruh. Diadu secara<br />barbar di atas ring melawan gladiator raksasa. Pertarungan dahsyat dengan<br />menggunakan sejumlah jurus wushu yang mendebarkan pun digelar.<br /><br />Perjalanan itu begitu panjang dan melelahkan. Menembus belukar di antara<br />desingan peluru. Menyusuri daratan ranjau. Disana dia betemu Epona, gadis<br />penakluk ranjau. Disana pula ia bertemu kembali dengan Kell. Lalu, pada<br />sebuah kunjungan ke lokasi ranjau, tattoo ke 618, angka kebebasan paripurna<br />Kell, dirajahkan. Dalam dialog cerdas, konyol, menggelikan, dan bertabur air<br />mata. Adegan mengejutkan, dan merupakan bagian terindah. Kebebasan itu<br />datang dan menyapa dalam damai. Nikmati adegan ini sambil mendengarkan You<br />Take My Breath Away-nya QUEEN. Berani sumpah, kau akan hening berjam-jam<br />sesudahnya...</span>
  <a data-text-id="3071506154848273491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

<a href="/questions/609120-sempat-terlintas-pertanyaan-di-benakku">Sempat terlintas pertanyaan di benakku, kenapa novel kedua dari Supernova diberi judul Akar? Judul yang baik tentu dapat mengundang rasa penasaran bukan? Yup, dari sanalah aku kembali berkubang dengan yang dipikir dan sempat terpikir oleh Dee untuk menemukan jawabannya. Tidak begitu nampak korelasi antara buku ini dengan serial yang pertama, Kesatria, Putri dan Bintang Jatuh.</a>

        <a title="Irwan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irwan" href="/user/show/183639-irwan">Irwan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5035827" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13898378516680109413">A popular Indonesian novel. I read the prequel of this trilogy (?). I cant remember much from the previous one. I am quite sure I had a good time and was impressed reading it. I remember an expression "badai serotonin", the serotonin storm! Not bad!<br/><br/>Having said that, I found it difficult to enter the realm of this novel until I changed my attitude to the one I use when I read a scifi/fantasy novel. The striking quality of this novel is its inovative creativity, sometimes bordering ambitious. It i</span>
  <span id="freeText13898378516680109413" style="display:none">A popular Indonesian novel. I read the prequel of this trilogy (?). I cant remember much from the previous one. I am quite sure I had a good time and was impressed reading it. I remember an expression "badai serotonin", the serotonin storm! Not bad!<br /><br />Having said that, I found it difficult to enter the realm of this novel until I changed my attitude to the one I use when I read a scifi/fantasy novel. The striking quality of this novel is its inovative creativity, sometimes bordering ambitious. It is like the author wants to say a lot of things - covering a lot of grounds, achieving universal grandeur - at the same time. <br /><br />The use of analogy and metaphors is, though naughtily creative, sometimes weird. "Menatap rambutnya seperti makan bubur ketan hitam: gelap, padat, wangi", "Perbukitan hijau itu tampak seperti meja bilyar diseraki butiran Nutrisari". I tried hard to imagine what kind of effect or images intended to arise in the reader's mind. <br /><br />Description of tattoing process, a wushu style called chang quan (which I happened to practice a long time ago), or Bodhi as a character are some of the achievements of this work.<br /><br />If I were the author, I wouldn't be too generous with foreign words. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13898378516680109413" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_62230171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/62230171" />
    <a title="Doofenshmirtz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2488160-doofenshmirtz"><img alt="Doofenshmirtz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246829954p2/2488160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/62230171?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Doofenshmirtz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Doofenshmirtz" href="/user/show/2488160-doofenshmirtz">Doofenshmirtz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2488160-doofenshmirtz?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2488160-doofenshmirtz?shelf=indo">indo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer62230171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14690582014344607390">I didn't like the book at all; it was too sloppily written. It was as if the author wrote whatever came to her mind and never bothered with a little process called "editing." There is also the interview I recall reading in which the author admitted to not being a big reader, which boggled my mind to no end. To be a good writer, one has to at least like to read. What, did she publish this book as a joke? (What saddens me, of course, is the fact of how popular her books ended up being. How is this</span>
  <span id="freeText14690582014344607390" style="display:none">I didn't like the book at all; it was too sloppily written. It was as if the author wrote whatever came to her mind and never bothered with a little process called "editing." There is also the interview I recall reading in which the author admitted to not being a big reader, which boggled my mind to no end. To be a good writer, one has to at least like to read. What, did she publish this book as a joke? (What saddens me, of course, is the fact of how popular her books ended up being. How is this even possible?)<br /><br />As much as I commend the author's attempt at covering subjects she may not know much about, it bothered me that she actually tried to pass "peremuk tulang" as a legitimate martial arts move. Does anyone else not remember Kung Fu Boy starring Chinmi? This move was taken straight from that manga series! I mean, if this book was meant to be humorous I would have laughed it off, but Supernova was supposed to be deep and philosophical. It's just... wrong. It's possibly plagiarism, but mostly it's just wrong. <br /><br />'Nuff said, I'm off now ranting about some other book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14690582014344607390" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3378636302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14770764294963151424">It's not what I expected. I thought there would be another episode of Reuben and Dimas creating another character. But no, it's a new main character on his own story. <br/><br/>Surprisingly, the storyline is much better than the first one! The adventure, the friendship, the fantasy. I like it!<br/><br/>Some part is not so enjoyable to read, but at least it's not some telenovela-kind-of script like the first book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7758614381539988538" style="display:none">Ok, after the first book, lemme continue with the second book: Supernova Akar:)<br />Actually, this is the first book of Supernova series that I read. I remember at that time I have heard about Supernova for quite a long time but I wasn't interested to read this as I was a bit skeptical about Indonesian literature. Yet, after reading this book, I changed my perspective about Supernova especially and Indonesian literature generally.<br />This book is about a journey. It tells the story of a man who has no parents named Bodi (Is this the correct spelling? Sorry, I don't remember&gt;.&lt;). As he doesn't know about himself (he was left in front of a Buddha temple when he was a baby), he started his journey to search himself. At the end, he didn't find his history but I think he found something bigger than that. <br />Don't think that journey will make this book boring. Bodi's journey is coloured with many exciting matters. From working as a tattoist in Thailand, tattoing a naked beautiful girl in her ****** (hehehehe^__^), working as opium harvester in Golden Triangle, until being chased by Khmer Rouge soldier in Kamboja.<br />From his journey, we can learn about life as well as this is one of the central topic that I think Dee wants to discuss. Here we can learn how to face life and then to face its end.<br />The end of this book is unclear, full with mistery. Understandable, because this book will continue to the next book, Supernova Petir<br />Read this book! It is nice. It is so different from the previous book; don't get surprised:). Not so complicated but can be very deep. </span>

  <span id="freeText12708239391465145449" style="display:none">It took a year for me to finish the book because after I read the first chapter, I stopped and put it in the box for almost a year. At first, I wasn't interested to continue reading the book because it seemed unrelated to the first book. Different from the first book which mix science theories with romance and drama with lovable characters, this second book has very unique character. <br /><br />The main character is very unique, or odd I can say. Bodhi, a bald guy with abnormal head bone structure and seems having supernatural ability. <br /><br />But when I got into the two third part of the book, it is getting interesting. The unique character and his adventures to accomplish a mission (which until the ending is still not clear) makes me really curious. <br /><br />This book leads me to the next series to figure out what's the relation between Diva (from the first book), Bodhi and Supernova.<br /> </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4975075364910959241">I really love this book. I love traveling, and this book gives me the sensation of backpackers' pleasure.<br/><br/>Ms. Dewi Lestari has succeeded in telling me a funny, endearing tale about Bodhi, a guy who's weird in an extraordinary way. Great story told in her great style of writing, both of which I give my admiration.<br/><br/>Bodhi has definitely become one of my favorite fictional characters! :)</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IZ3dqFoeFxQ4NoNGZ2BbSz8wn8yeBGyjLDhNL00VtEYzmZeMyqsKGOJJDnG+ilusMah34eignrSHk98DytR7UQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('i5ByL9JhZ24hJFSmNkYEMMliIPHrPUdNgnyAjbzmSJSZlDgLQtR6Yvtb2ZHvrATXx/rI3J2ZtVop1xKhOyeHgw==')})
  }

It is at o­nce an exposé of the oppression of plantation workers in South Sumatra, a lyrical quest to understand the place of religion and spirituality in contemporary lives, a playful exploration of female sexuality and a story about love in all its guises, while touching o­n all of Indonesia’s taboos: extramarital sex, political repression and the relationship between Christians and Muslims.Saman has taken the Indonesian literary world by storm and sold over 100,000 copies in the Indonesian language, and is now available for the first time in English.ABOUT THE AUTHORAyu Utami was born in Bogor, grew up in Jakarta and obtained her bachelor degree in Literature Studies from University of Indonesia. She worked as a journalist for Matra, Forum Keadilan, and D&amp;R. Not long after the New Order regime closed Tempo, Editor, and Detik, she participated in the founding of Indonesia’s Alliance of Independent Journalists to protest the closure of those three weeklys. Currently she is working for the cultural journal Kalam, and at Teater Utan Kayu. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10368601546114462439">Dee Lestari, is one of the bestselling and critically acclaimed writers in Indonesia.<br/>Born in January 20, 1976, she began her debut with a serial novel: Supernova in 2001. Supernova’s first episode, <i>Kesatria, Putri, dan Bintang Jatuh</i> (The Knight, The Princess, and The Falling Star), was sold phenomenally, achieving a cult status among Indonesian young readers. She has published four other episodes:</span>
  <span id="freeText10368601546114462439" style="display:none">Dee Lestari, is one of the bestselling and critically acclaimed writers in Indonesia.<br />Born in January 20, 1976, she began her debut with a serial novel: Supernova in 2001. Supernova’s first episode, <i>Kesatria, Putri, dan Bintang Jatuh</i> (The Knight, The Princess, and The Falling Star), was sold phenomenally, achieving a cult status among Indonesian young readers. She has published four other episodes: <i>Akar</i> (The Root), <i>Petir</i> (The Lightning), <i>Partikel</i>(The Particle), and <i>Gelombang</i> (The Wave). <br />Aside of the Supernova series, Dee has also published a novel titled <i>Perahu Kertas</i> (Paper Boat), and three anthologies: <i>Filosofi Kopi</i> (Coffee’s Philosophy), <i>Madre</i>, and <i>Rectoverso</i> — a unique hybrid of music and literature. <br />Dee also has an extensive music career, producing four albums with her former vocal trio, and two solo albums. She has been writing songs for renowned Indonesian artists. <br /><i>Perahu Kertas</i> (Paper Boat) was turned into a movie in 2009, marking Dee’s debut as a screenplay writer. The movie became one of the national's block busters. Following the same path, <i>Madre, Filosofi Kopi, Madre,</i> and <i>Supernova KPBJ,</i> were made into movies. <br />In February 2016, Dee released the final episode of Supernova, <i>Inteligensi Embun Pagi</i> (Intelligence of the Morning Dew). All Dee’s books are published by Bentang Pustaka. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10368601546114462439" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
